The man died about three days, and I had been summoned to remove it; I saw the size of the stone and the condition of the urine, estimating what I witnessed.
I saw another doctor who was supporting himself among some of our local military leaders with medicine.
I saw a black slave who had a fracture near the ankle with an injury to him, and the doctor, in his haste, tightened the fracture on the wound using ligatures and clamps tightly without allowing the wound to breathe.
Then he indulged him in his desires, then left him for days and ordered him not to use the ligature until his leg and foot swelled up and he was at risk of death.

The first gate.
In the kidney.
And before we mention its use, it should be mentioned how to benefit from and its drawbacks, and in what mood it is used.
I say, the discussion about how to benefit from the kidney and its drawbacks is a long topic with precise knowledge and hidden secrets, in which many wise people have spoken.
And they differed on it. I have shortened their brief discourse for fear of going into unnecessary length.
I say, the kidney benefits generally for every bad mood that occurs with or without a substance as a catalyst. There are two types of such moods: one is the hot mood without substance and the other is the dry mood without substance.
Now, if it's the dry mood with a substance, they have differed on it. Some say that the kidney benefits in such cases, while others disagree stating that the kidney is not suitable for a disease resulting from heat and dryness because of the nature of fire being characterized by heat and dryness.
And it's impossible to derive treatment for a disease that is both hot and dry with a medicine that is also hot and dry. The one who argues against this states that the kidney can be beneficial when exposed to fire, treating diseases that are both hot and dry which occur in human bodies. Because if you add the body and its moisture to the fire mood, it will result in the body becoming cold.
And I say as he says, because experience has shown me that. But it shouldn't be imagined in this matter unless one has consented and navigated through the door of the kidney extensively. Stop to consider the differences in people's dispositions and conditions of their diseases within themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for other moods, there is no fear of them for you and certainly not for the cold wet diseases, all physicians agree on them and they do not differ in the benefit of garlic for them.
Know, my sons, that there is the benefit of treatment with fire and its superiority to treatment with burned medicine because fire is a single essence that does not exceed the function of an organ in which it affects or harms another connected organ only slightly.
And treatment with burned medicine might go beyond its function to later organs and may cause a disease within the organ that is difficult to cure, or it may kill. But because of the dignity and generosity of fire's essence, this only happens if it has been overdone.
And we have understood that through experience due to the long service, care for craftsmanship, and standing on the facts of the matter.
For this reason, I refrained from lengthening the discussion even though it would be fitting for my book if I had included a secret and mysterious aspect of fire and how it operates in bodies and its absence from diseases with philosophical proof that validates understanding.
Know, my sons, that they have disagreed on the time when garlic should be used and declared that the best time is during spring.
And I say that garlic can be used at all times because the harm caused by time gets absorbed in the benefit brought about by garlic. And especially if garlic is from necessary strong pains that cannot tolerate delay, for fear that it might follow with a worse problem than the internal harm caused by time.
Do not let the people and the uneducated doctors confuse you, my sons, that the worm which cures a disease will never recur and make it into an infamous entity.
Neither is the worm, which they imagined to have the capability of changing moods and drying out moisture, which is a cause of pains.
Yet the worm prefers over medicine in terms of the speed of its success, strength of its action, and intensity of its sovereignty.
However, the illness might return at some time according to the patient's mood and the success of their disease and its strength, as well as what accumulates in his body due to negligence in acquiring food and so on, among other causes.
O God, let the disease that uses worms be a gentle one and in an organ with little moisture and dampness. Like the worm that relieves pain and such, it may be possible that this pain does not recur, which would be at least a relief.
As for the general public's statement that the worm is the last resort of medicine, it is a correct saying not in line with what they believe because they think there is no cure that can benefit either with or without medication after getting the worm, which goes against this.
The meaning of "the worm is the last resort" simply means that if we have tried various treatments for a disease without success, then we use the worm as a final treatment which does work. Therefore, here lies the reason why 'the worm' is considered the last resort in medicine. Not according to the interpretation that many people and some uneducated doctors have arrived at.
I have mentioned that gold is better than iron, and they said this because of the balance of gold and the nobility of its essence. They also claimed that it does not corrode the place where it's applied, which is absolutely false.
Because I tried it and found that it works in some bodies but not in others. The one made of gold is better than iron as they said, except that if you heated the anvil in fire with gold, you wouldn't be able to tell when it reaches the temperature needed for redness of the gold.
And because it accelerates cooling; if you increase its heat in fever, it melts in fire and it can cause confusion for the craftsman. Therefore, iron is faster and closer to perfection in our work, if Allah wills.

The first section.
In the head, there is one type of treatment.
This type of treatment is useful for combating moisture and cold that affect the brain, both causes of headaches, frequent headcold symptoms going from the head to the eyes and ears area, excessive sleepiness, toothaches, and sore throats. The process of this treatment involves initially instructing the patient to undergo three or four nights of bowel cleansing with a gentle head-clearing medicine, depending on their strength, age and habits.

Then place the base of your palm on the tip of his nose between his eyes. Where your middle finger ends, mark that position with ink.
Then heat the oil-based wax as shown here.
Lift your hand if the size of the shoulder joint opening is as big as a man's head or as big as a pomegranate seed. If it is cold, repeat with the same hammer or with another one if it has cooled down. Until you see what was explained to you from the bone, then take some salt and dissolve it in water. Put a cotton ball into it and drink its contents. Place the cotton on the site and leave it for three days.
Then, apply a cotton ball soaked in oil to him until the burnt smell disappears. Then heal him with the four ointments until he recovers, if God wills.

Chapter Twenty-One.
In cases of gum pain.
If gum pain is due to cold or there are worms inside and treatment with medicines did not work, the approach includes two methods: either treating with fat or treating with fire.
As for treating with fat, you would take the cow's fat and boil it in a iron pot or a sieve. Then take cotton thread and tie it at one end of the heated rod. Then dip it in the boiling fat and place it on the painful tooth using the wheel to hold it until it cools down.
Then repeat it several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. Or if you prefer, you can dip wool or cotton in cold fat and place it on the painful tooth, then put the heated wheel above it so that the fire reaches the base of the tooth.
And if it is treated with fire, this means using a copper or iron tube. There should be some wax in its core to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the opening of the scar. Then light the lamp that comes out of its shape and place it on the same incision while holding your hand until the lamp cools down. Do this several times.
And the pain either goes away that day, or another day. After this, it is necessary for him to fill the scar with good tallow and hold it for an hour, then throw it away; this is the shape of the lamp.
You can apply it to any part you want and according to what is possible, this is the shape of the tube.

If by fire, then it consists in heating the dried cork brush resembling an eagle's feather made of iron around each side of the nail and making sure that its edges are thin. Then dip this into a protective mixture on the nail and rotate your hand with the hot iron around the nail until you reach to the depth of the nail.
He leaves it for three days to heal, then strengthens the pus with boiled bread dough that has been salted and allows the dressing to stay on overnight. It then peels off from its roots and he treats the wound site with aloe vera ointment until it heals, if the nails are not reversed.
Many times, it occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. It is necessary to take a copper pipe or one made of iron or eagle's feathers, lower it onto the nail or hole, then pour a little hot water into the pipe.
Hold your hand and gently wiggle it while turning the pipe, causing the edge of the pipe to affect the root of the nail. The hot water then finds its way into the root of the nail, allowing the affected person a brief moment of discomfort from the hot water for a minute.
Then leave it, for the nail will come out with its roots. Do this to each one until you have dealt with all of them in the body. After they have come out, treat the areas with ointments that promote flesh growth.
The forty-fifth chapter.
In the case of popping noise.
If a popping sensation occurs in one of the nerves, or from a quarter fever or any other condition, it should be treated by heating four or five rods on the back between each rod of heat treatment, and in his chest area as well. And on his stomach, apply heat with an oil lamp iron, for the popping sensation subsides and speeds up the maturation of the cold illness.
The fifty-fifth chapter.
In cases where there is bleeding in the body.
Perhaps in the body, eruptions can occur which are disgusting masses made from cold, firm, rotten materials. It is necessary for these first appearances to be contained on top of every small, curative blister using a reed that has been lit at its tip or with a long tongs or with a convex lens hammer.
The pus may be contained in its first eruption on this condition, so it does not increase and the effectiveness of it dissipates, and it is cleared from impurity except that it should be after removing the impurity with scratching.
The Sixty-Fifth Chapter.
In cases of acute bleeding upon cutting the artery.
Bleeding often occurs from an artery that has been severed during a cut exposed to the outside, or upon making a slit in a tumor, or similar cases, and it is difficult to cut it.
If this happens to anyone, quickly move your hand towards the mouth of the artery and place your little finger on it, gently pulling until the blood is contained under your finger and nothing escapes from there. Then put a few small and large cotton wicks that are greased in fire until they become very hot.
Then, take one of them, either small or large depending on the wound and where the artery was severed. Place the iron onto the same vein after quickly removing your finger with a wheel and holding the iron until the bleeding stops.
If, upon lifting your finger from the mouth of the artery and extinguishing the iron, you take another iron with a wheel from the prepared greased iron rods. Continue doing this with one after another until the bleeding stops.
Preserve, do not burn the nerve. There are alternative explanations for what you hear on auscultation, and understand that if blood flows from a vessel, it cannot be cut under any circumstances, especially if the vessel is large, except with one of four methods: either by ligation as we said or by amputation if it has not been cauterized. If it is amputated, its ends contract and the blood flow stops. Alternatively, it can be ligated tightly with threads or, alternatively, medications that tend to stop the blood flow and tight binding by the forceps are applied.
As for those who attempt to cut it with a ligature or by tightening with the force, or placing burned objects and so forth, it does not stop there at all except in rare cases. If one exposes any of that without having a doctor or medicine present, he should pinch the index finger against the wound itself as we described.
He should tighten it greatly until the blood is squeezed and escapes from above the wound, on the vessel and the finger. The bleeding does not stop with cold water for an extremely long time until the blood congeals and hardens, and then it stops. During this period, you need to check whether you need a clamp or medicine.
The second chapter.
In the case of the cut, burn, fracture and surgeries, etc.
He said, Al-Khwarizmi mentioned in the first chapter all diseases that can be treated with fire and burned medicine, along with their reasons, causes, tools, and examples of burning equivalents. This was done as separate sections throughout history from antiquity to modern times.
And I follow this path in this chapter with the same method, making it easier for the student to achieve what is required...
Before I proceed with this, you my sons should know that in this section there are many complexities beyond what is contained within this section alone.
And for that reason, the caution should be stricter in this section because the work in this field often leads to the depletion of blood which supports life when a wound is opened or incision made on a tumor, an extraction from the body, surgery treatment, removal of an arrow or incision through a stone and so forth. These all come with many complications and fears and death occurs in most of them.
And I advise you to beware of what might cause doubt among you, for in this profession there are many people with various illnesses; some have become hardened by their illness and the death has humiliated them.
Due to the severity of their suffering and the length of their illnesses, as well as the impact of their illness on determining what indicates death, among them are those who have spent your money in hopes for recovery from you when their illness is deadly; they will not die easily. It should not be that you assist one who has this particular trait heavily.
Let your caution be stronger than your desire and concern. Do not proceed with anything of that without solid proof and certainty that it leads to the desired outcome. Use in all treatment for your illness, the advancement of knowledge and warning about what leads to safety.
In that, you will have support for gaining praise and glory, remembrance and gratitude. May Allah inspire you my sons to guide right direction, do not restrict yourselves from rectitude and success, as only He has control over it; there is no god but Him.

The First Chapter.
In the treatment of water that gathers at the heads of infants.
This particular type of scabies often affects infants at birth, if the midwife presses on the baby's head without gentleness. It may also occur for an unknown hidden reason that is not known.
I have not seen this cause in anyone other than infants, and all of those I saw from them died quickly, which is why I stopped practicing it. And among them was an infant whose head was full of water, and the head increased every day. Until he couldn't bear to sit on himself because of the size of his head and the moisture increased until it caused death.
This moisture either collects between the skin and bone, or gathers under the bone on the scalp. The treatment in case the moisture is within the skin and bone, and if the tumor is small, it's necessary to make a single incision across the head until the moisture drains out. This is an image of how this operation was performed.
If the moisture is more and the tumor is larger, make two intersecting incisions like this:
And if the moisture is under the bone and its sign is that you can see scalp wrinkles from every side, water will decrease when you squeeze it with your hand inside; it should not be hidden from you. It's necessary to make three incisions in the middle of the head like this:
After making the incision, all moisture is drained. The wounds are then tightened with sutures and bandages. At day five, water and oil are applied from above until the headband is removed. Then, the wound is treated with ointments and poultices without over-tightening the headband or feeding the patient only dry food with low moisture content.
Until the member strengthens and heals, another prescription is to observe where the bone of the tumor appears and the convergence of water because it may be at the back of the head more or in its front or on the right or in the north.
You are referring to the incision where the tumor is visible to you and the water accumulation, so you make an incision as much as possible and observe that you might cut a vessel causing bleeding. This bleeding will lead to the death of the patient due to that hemorrhage, along with the expulsion of moisture.
The second chapter.
Cutting the two vessels that are behind the ears, known as the hissiyis.
When someone experiences severe attacks affecting both eyes or the chest, and if medications have failed to provide relief after this point, inform about resorting to treating by cutting these two vessels.
If you wish to cut them, you should shave the patient's head according to Moses' method, then scrape the area with a coarse tool so that the vessel becomes visible. Then you should tighten the neck of the patient by pulling their cloak, and look where the veins pulse and their locations, the two prominent places behind the ears which are mostly exposed except in some people.
Then, learn the insertion points on them with a needle, and cut them with the cauterizing forceps down to the bone. This can be done across the head, but if you wish, you can insert the forceps from under the vessel up to above by cutting, and the length of the cut will be about two inches.
If the sweat, once interrupted, starts to bleed in a pulsating manner heading forward and spreading to the chest and body. If the vessel is not visible through touch, it might be necessary to estimate its location from behind the ear after counting three fingers. Then learn with a needle and cut until reaching the bone. It should be noted that...
Blood is sent through six routes of the medium and might send more or less, all according to your perception of the strength of the patient and the filling of their arteries. Then look at the wound; if there remains a piece of the fracture within the wound, cut it off.
To avoid exposure to a hot tumor, then bind the wound with a wick of cotton thread followed by treatment with ointments until it heals.
Chapter Three.
Suturing the two vessels in the grooves.
If someone experiences recurrent or sudden outbreaks due to dry heat and fever affecting the muscles of the grooves or severe chronic headache, among others, and various medical treatments fail to alleviate this, we have tried bleeding by puncturing the vessels in the grooves or their vicinity as described.
The purpose of bleeding is to shave the hair on the grooves, which refers to the visible vessel in the groove. From its pulsation, you can determine most things as only a few are hidden even among people.
Or when the cold is severe, it may hide from you. In this case, have the patient support his neck with a thick garment. Then mark the location with a wick or heat the area with hot water until the vessel becomes visibly and clearly present. Then take the scalpel, which is what it looks like. Then, using it very gently, you strip away the skin until you reach the vessel. After that, you place a string and pull it upwards so that it comes out of the skin. You remove any clots underneath from all sides. If the vessel is thin, twist its end with the string. Then remove part of it until the two ends are far apart and constrict, without causing bleeding. If it does not fall off or break, blood will not flow at all, then remove the blood from six to three places.
If the vein is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong doubled thread. The thread may be either from hemp or from the strings of the violin so that dirt does not reach the wound before the injury heals and causes bleeding.
Then cut a preference between the ligatures. Do this at that time or after another period, and if you want, seal it with iron using an iron knife until its ends fall off. This operation takes place exactly as described or better, as we said.
However, if there is fever or mood swings in the affected area because iron helps eliminate moisture, it becomes more effective and benefits better. It should be filled with dry cotton after tying both veins, and placed with tight ligatures. After healing, it is treated with medicinal herbs that promote wound healing, and vinegar until it heals, God willing.
If bleeding occurs during your work from the vein, proceed to cut it either with iron or fill the area with a ligature and tighten your hand until the blood stops. If this does not stop the bleeding, place your finger until the blood clots.
And let the area be cooled with intense cold water until the pain subsides and tighten as necessary, which is lighter and easier than tying both veins using this iron knife after learning their positions with the thread.
And lower it very gently until it reaches the bone and the sweat stops in two places so that what is between its ends can separate, for it will not adhere to this iron at all. This is an image of the iron knife.
The sharpness of the scalpel resembles that of two small needles, except it is much less sharper than a scalpel. If they were both as sharp as a scalpel, cold would come faster to them and the cutting of flesh wouldn't stop quickly. But if there is some hardness in them, fire's heat will stick on them.
The flesh was cut quickly, this work is better than every other action and it's lighter and easier. Let there be the thickness of a finger between the blades for hardness.
The Fourth Chapter.
In the treatment of excessive, constant flow of hot tears to the eyes.
If tears are constant and the flow comes from the channels on the forehead from outside, without any benefit from medical treatment with medicines, I saw the face of the unfortunate person had become reddened. He feels a stinging sensation on his forehead like that of an insect bite, and both his eyes are hanging wetted. His eyelids have become swollen from the intensity of tears which have soaked them. Faced with this, the first resort in its treatment is this act, they call it sword medicine. It involves having the unfortunate person shave off the hair on their forehead.
Then, three cuts are made on the forehead. These cuts run parallel to each other along the forehead. The length of each cut is approximately the length of an inch, with one cut aligned parallel to the nose in the center of the forehead, the second slightly behind the muscle movement at the jaw, and the third on the opposite side.
Be careful not to cut the two veins on the sides. Keep your hand away from where the jaws connect. Leave three inches between each cut and have a sponge or a wet wipe ready, as they will soak up blood.
Then the sharp forceps, which is depicted in this picture, is introduced. From the cut following the bite to the central cut, all the skin between the two cuts is peeled off along with the inflammation on the bone. This procedure is also done from the central cut to the third cut, and then this forceps is removed. Another device is also introduced in the first cut, called a sharp scalpel on one side and smooth but not sharp on the other. This is its picture:.
She makes her sharp side towards the flesh attached to the skin and her smooth side towards the bone, pushing it until she reaches the central cut, cutting with it all the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes without reaching the surface of the skin.
Then, she performs this in the middle cut to the other cut, after letting out an amount of blood considered moderate, she squeezes the places with clotted blood. Then, for each cut, she inserts a cotton thread and applies a poultice made from a drink, oil or honey and oil on it.
In order to prevent a hot tumor, on the third day the bandage is removed and she uses a lot of wet cotton wool. Then, it is treated with the basilics ointment with rose oil and other remedies used for wounds until it heals if God willing.
Chapter Five.
In the treatment of tears and discharges to the eyes from inside the head.
When one experienced frequent severe discharges, you see his eyes drooping and tiny, with weakened vision. The eyelids are swollen and the eyebrows are falling out. In the depth of the head, there is an intense sharp pain and continuous coughing. From these symptoms, it should be known that such substances and discharges come from numerous deep veins. The best treatment in such cases is this method: order the sick person to shave their forehead then make a single cut down the middle of the forehead.
In the depth of the head, there is an intense sharp pain and continuous coughing. From these symptoms, it should be known that such substances and discharges come from numerous deep veins. The best treatment in such cases is this method: order the sick person to shave their forehead then make a single cut down the middle of the forehead. Or lift it slightly upwards and start the cut from the left corner of the mouth to the right corner of the mouth. The cut should go towards the bone, and when you hold your hand away from the moving muscles near the jaw while chewing until the bone is exposed and all blood is wiped up with a sponge.
Separate the edges of the incision with a cotton thread or a cotton thread, then pull from above using the sutures and soak the sutures in water and oil to prevent a hot lump from forming. Once you have cleared it, if you see that the hot lump has disappeared, it is necessary to cut into the bone so that new tissue begins to grow.
Then, treat it with a dried process that promotes tissue growth like taking two parts of buckwheat flour and four parts of thyme. Prepare a paste from them and use it to promote tissue growth in such surgeries.
The Sixth Chapter.
In the treatment of what falls into the ear.
All that falls into the ear is of four kinds: either a metallic rock like iron or glass, or a plant seed like chickpeas and kernels, etc., or something liquid such as water and vinegar, etc.
And if it's an animal, when a stone or something similar to the stone that doesn't grow in the ear falls into the ear, receive the ear towards sunlight. If you see that the stone has become somewhat greasy with some almond oil or camphor oil, then try to remove it by moving your head or blowing out with a feather. Stopping the ear leaks after coughing when a string of leather or wool is placed around the ear and the ear is pulled upwards. This treatment often results in its removal if it doesn't, then try to remove it with a gentle pick as depicted here.
If it comes out with the pick, otherwise try to remove it with a slightly curved blunt awl. If it doesn't come out from that either, make an asbest and insert one end of the tube into the ear hole deeply.
Seal around the tube with oiled plaster so that there is no path for the wind except through the tube, then pull it with your breath strongly and frequently. Often enough it will come out in this way, if it doesn't come out as we described and instead take a little from honey or finely prepared bird food which is used to catch birds and place it at the end of the applicator.
After tightly wrapping it around, then gently insert it into the ear hole after wiping out moisture from the ear. If it doesn't come out even after all that we've described, proceed to make an incision before a hot tumor or twitching occurs.
The incision recipe is to cut the wax in the ear canal first and bleed it according to its strength, then place the wax between your hands and turn its back upwards. Make a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat is located on the lower part.
The incision should be in a crescent shape until you reach the stone, then remove it as much as possible with tools. Then stitch up the cut quickly and treat it until it heals.
If the thing falling in your ear is one of the seeds that grow and inflate, try to remove it with what was mentioned. If this doesn't work for removal, take a fine, delicate burr as shown here.
Try to remove this type of falling seeds from the ear. If you are certain that this seed has become moistened with the ear vapor until it becomes many small pieces, then remove it using the dark lamp or a soft brush or by suction.
As we mentioned, it makes it easier to remove. As for water in the ear, it should be expelled using coughing on a camphor stick first. If he is lying down with something of old cotton stuffed into his ear, then if he is able to expel it through this method.
Otherwise, take a large number of small sand grains along your fingers and heat them with fire slightly. Then, insert one of these camphor pieces into his ear and blow on one of his feet from that side. Strike another stone on the stone in the ear.
He continues doing this with grain after grain until all the water is removed. Water can be expelled by taking one of the goose feathers or ice, inserting only one end into the ear and heating the other end with fire until most of it burns. Then another feather is repeated.
You do this several times until all the water is removed or it is sucked out with a tube as described earlier in the sand section. As for removing any animal that might be inside, observe if its body size is small like a fish and similar objects; then you should use what was mentioned in the division for such cases.
If its body is large and can be felt with the hand, try to remove it using a soft brush and tubes; this will make it easier than all other things that might occur in the ear. As for removing the wax worm from the ear if you treated it as described in our section on insects without wax, then your treatment did not succeed.
You should look into the ear towards the sun, if you see a bit of wax, remove it with tweezers or fine forceps. If you do not see anything from them, take this tube to picture its image.
It is narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. Insert a delicate tip into the ear to the extent that it can bear, then insert the strong hook inside the ear. Do this several times until all wax comes out. If no progress for its removal, seal around the tube with candles as I explained to you in case of stone.
If the wax does not come out as we have described, use the devices I mentioned. These were first tried in removing wax and you will find them explained in an article about these instruments. Using this machine allows for pouring of medicines or oils into the ear like this: [illustration provided]
As you see, it is made of silver or brass. It's narrow at the bottom with a small hole and wide at the top. If desired, the pump inside the tube can be made of tight-fitting brass. Alternatively, you can take a hollow reed and wrap it tightly on its tip with a piece of string.
Then pour the oil or juice or any other medicine you want into the tube, and then place it in the ear. Insert the wick of cotton from above and squeeze it moderately with your hand until the oil flows into the auditory canal, which will feel good.
Place the wick inside, and ensure that whatever you place in the ear has been slightly warmed by fire. Be careful not to let the substance that rotates within it be too cold or excessively hot. The ear cannot tolerate this.
Chapter Seven.
In the treatment of wax blockage in the ear.
Some children may exit their mothers' wombs and their ears' canals unscarred.
And it may also expose some individuals to a plug in the ear canal due to a wound or a新生 tissue there. This plug could be inside the depth of the ear hole, not visible by sight.
It may project slightly outside the hole and be visible. The one that is in depth of the ear but not visible usually makes it hard to see. The one that is visible, you should place the deaf's ear in the sun. Inspect it, and if you see the plug clearly, open it with a gentle pair of forceps; here's what this would look like:.
It will have a slightly protruding tip that is somewhat limited, and the rest of the forceps are smooth to avoid injuring the ear. If the plug is growing tissue in the ear canal, hold it with a soft hook and cut it gently until all the tissue is removed.
If the plug is in depth of the ear, take a gentle smooth probe and heat it slightly over fire. Then insert it into the ear canal. If you feel the plug along with what the deaf person experiences from loss of hearing, gently remove it carefully.
Be careful not to cut the eardrum, then place a wick in the ear up to the size of the hole that fits it properly. Do this for days until you are sure that there is no risk of wound healing or take a bit of the wick and dip it in water, then rub it with powdered zinc.
Use it if you see the ear has swollen and place a hot wick inside. It should be expected that you remove this wick and replace it with another one, which was soaked in camphor made from rose oil to soothe the hot swelling. Then treat it until it heals.
If there is bleeding, immerse a sponge or a hole in cold water and place it on the ear. Use all treatments that stop the mentioned bleeding as described in "The Book of Remedies".
The eighth chapter.
In treating the drops that appear on the cheeks.
These drops that appear on the eyelids may be wet or dry. They should be held with tweezers or pincers and cut from their roots using scissors. Then they should be placed in position with some powder.
If there is bleeding from it, treat it with a soft eyeglass forceps. It's better to do this after cutting and it often returns if there is something left of its roots. If you heat it with fire, those roots will be burned and it won't return.
The ninth chapter.
In treating the frost that appears on the cheeks of the eye.
Very often, there is something resembling frost in intensity and hardness on the cheeks of the eye.
And that's why it is called frost; it's the assembly of thick moisture in the upper and lower eyelids. The work here is to look, if you find the frost protruding from the eyelid, move towards every side; thus, treating it is easy; you just have to cut through it with a horizontal incision.
Then, gently scrape it from every side until you remove it completely. Hang it with pincers and cut it. If you can't cut it right away after the cutting of the eyelid, this does not harm anything in your absence. If the incision is large, stitch it together and treat it until it heals.
And if it's small, don't worry about it; the ointment will push and bind it. If the eyelid is inclined towards the inner eyelid towards the inside surface, turn the eyelid and hang the lid with a loop without needing to cut and pierce it from every side.
And if you remove the eyelid by cutting, it will not harm. Then wash the eye with salty water after removing the lid and treat the area with something that binds until the eye heals.
The Tenth Chapter.
In treating the condition of double eyelid that appears in the eyelid.
The double eyelid is a patch that forms in the layers of the upper eyelid. This condition mostly affects boys, making their eyes look heavy and prone to suffering from frequent night sweats. They often cannot bear to look at sunlight. In order that tears hasten towards them.
Therefore, you see them always reclining on their faces and they sleep with that position. Their eyelids under the eyebrows are wet due to frequent tears caused by this condition. The double eyelid is very obvious; when you touch the area between them with your fingers, you can feel it. The purpose of the operation is for the patient to place his head in a hole made in your seat during the process.
Then, take a thread of cotton and make from it a wick. Create a circle with that wick as large as what surrounds the double eyelid on all sides. Place it on the affected area and pinch it from all sides using your fingers to gather the extra skin in the center of the circle.
Then, cut through the center of this wet area with a cutting device (mbabus al-nashel) making a horizontal incision. The width of the cut should not be larger than the seam in the eyelid. In depth, it is necessary to cut all the skin down to the double eyelid.
In most cases, the cornea protrudes from the incision in the form of a piece of white fat. You then use a tool to pull it out between your fingers and take care to move your hand back and forth so as to free it, being careful not to cut too deeply to avoid damaging the eye with the forceps.
If the cornea does not appear in the first incision, it may be necessary to increase the depth of the cut slightly and gently until the cornea appears. Then you can pull it out as we have described, then dip a tool in vinegar and water, place it on the spot, and tighten it with a clamp. Some people press it with salt.
He places it in the cavity of the cut so that what remains of this moisture dissolves. Then he treats it until it heals. If there was an injury and a hot substance occurred at the site, he treated it with soothing ointment until it healed.
The eleventh chapter.
In the methods of ophthalmic surgery.
If a supernumerary eyelash grows outside the natural path beneath the natural lashes in the eye lid, it can harm the eye and cause various illnesses such as constant tearing, drooping of the eyebrows, whitening and cloudiness, to the extent that this becomes a cause for the loss of vision.
Eyebrow surgery can be done in four ways: either by burning with fire as explained in the section on fire, or by using a strong medicine as mentioned earlier, or it can be done through cutting and suturing, or using thread as I have described.
You should place the needle on your eyelid, then turn the eye lid with your left hand. If it turns properly, otherwise put in a needle from under the eyelash and pierce the needle with thread from above, making sure to pull the thread close to the hair itself and bring the thread up by pulling on the eyelash.
Turn it over with the scalpel, then cut into the inner lid skin beneath the excess hair by incising from the larger opening to the smaller one. Next, pull the thread and place a small cotton or linen pad under the eyelid, then stitch the lid shut.
Like the shape of an ace card, but it should be in proportion to how much you want to lift the eyelid because this can vary among people; some may need a cut from the eyelid that is suitably sized according to how relaxed the eyelid has become.
And some may require even less of this cut according to how relaxed the eyelid is, then you would incise with the scalpel along the two lines that you have marked and begin from the larger opening to the smaller one. The incision should be close to natural hair line as thin as a needle's prick.
Then, the needle enters one of the corners of the skin, then excises it all. The lips are stitched together with a needle and fine silk thread, wiping away the blood. Some things attached to eyebrows will be used to stick what is left of the threads on the eyebrows.
You may choose to do this or not, but it doesn't matter either way. The stitches and threads should remain in place for around three or four days before you proceed with the treatment. If desired, the wound can be left unsewn and treated with things that dry out and tighten; when the wound heals, lifting of the eyelid occurs at the site of closure, and stitching is indeed preferable.
This aspect of the surgery, I mentioned earlier, however it imposes some burden on the patient, but it works well and there is no danger involved. Another aspect in this procedure is that you stitch the eyelid in a shape like an ace card as described. Then the eyelid is lifted with three needles which may be separate or grouped like this image.
Then, the preferred part of the eyelid is cut with small scissors as shown in this image, cuts are made moderately:.
If you are unable to hold the needles, take an awl with a thread and insert it in the middle of this figure and insert another thread close to the inner corner and a third thread close to the outer corner, gather the threads between your fingers moderately then lift your hand slightly.
Then lift the taught skin as we have described. Sew both lips of the wound with stitches and heal it until it heals. If a heated lump appears when you cut or make incisions, treat that lump with camphor and other soothing ointments.
And the lower eyelid may also reverse its lashes, it should use what we mentioned about cutting and stitching and burning with fire or medicine, and burning with fire or medicine stronger yet milder than cutting and stitching in them I would do more careful.
Burning with the stick is done in this way; you flip the eyelid and cut the incision from inside as described, then make two or three pointed twigs of wood long along the length of the eyelid and shorter than the width of the pliers.
And I have borrowed from each end of both sides, where the threads stick. Then gather them gently on the preferred part of the eyelid and pull the twigs firmly from each side for a tightness and leave it for some days. The tightened skin dies, turns black and rots.
Until it leaves on its own, if it slows down, give her a loan then treat her until she recovers. If her fever decreases and the swelling of her eyelid does not diminish, these are the two eyelashes which you create in this manner and size with respect to length and width in each eye.
The second chapter.
In lifting the lost hair from the eye by using needles.
If it is a hair or two that need to be worked on, then take a fine needle and insert into it a thread of very fine silk that has been smoothed out. Then gather its ends and tie them with a very loose knot, let the length of the thread be about a yard.
Then place another fine thread in the needles shorter than it and tie its ends if you wish, then let the patient lie his head on your stone near the sun so that he can see the work well because it is a meticulous task. Then insert the needle into the root of the excessive hair with the threads.
And execute it on the eyelid with rapid strokes until it comes out above the natural hair. Then pull the thread up over the needles and enter that hair, whether it's one or two or three hairs no more.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out along with the needles in the eyelid together with the natural hair. If you pulled the needles and didn't extract the hair with them, you pulled the needles downwards with that thread which was fastened in the needles until they come out of the upper hole.
Then put the hair back in and pull it out again. Do this until it rises in the upper hole and you see it with the eye, then remove the needles and the thread and take them out and tighten the eye and leave it tight for two or three days until it binds the hair in its place and grows flesh on it.
If the stitch is short, either you add a long hair from your natural hair to it and it rises with it, or you leave it until it grows longer, then when that happens, you remove it.
The thirteenth chapter.
In the treatment of the hairrow that occurs in the upper eyelid.
The one affected by this hairrow is called an arnbia. This hairrow can be either natural or accidental. The accidental one results from a wound, a cut, or a tear, and so on.
The purpose of the treatment is to cut through this conglomeration and separate its two parts, making a thread appear between them. Then you should tie it until it heals. It's not advisable to use things that dry or tighten in her treatment.
If you do this, the hairrow will return more strongly than it was. Instead, use things that relax such as the loop and the tenter in water with a little soap and cotton syrup lotion dissolved in some oil, then apply it, treated it.
The essence of its treatment is to employ every trick not to reattach in the same form as it was initially. This action we mentioned, however, is some repair for the hairrow and not to return the condition of the place according to how it originally was.
The fourteenth chapter.
In the treatment of the hairrow that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This hairrow that occurs at the bottom is what we actually call a hairrow and can be natural or accidental. The accidental one results from a wound, a cut, or a tear, among other things.
The method in this is to take a needle with two threads within it, and pierce the flesh with it, then continue it from the left incision to the right until the thread becomes inside both parts of the flesh. Then raise the flesh above by means of the needle, and cut it with a broad scissor.
If the shape of the eyelid returns as it should, and otherwise if you take a thread and place it at the site of the cut and turn the eyelid with it to make two cuts in the inner side of the eyelid. The ends of these cuts come from the corners of the cut that was made until they meet forming an angle. Until if it has gathered, its shape becomes similar to this form:.
And it is the Greek letter lamda, then remove that flesh as much as its sharp side is below what follows the eyelid. Then gather the scattered parts with two threads and sew it with wool thread, then treat it with the medicines we mentioned for relaxation and swelling until it heals.
And if the swelling has spread from a cut or stitch or otherwise as should be, then make a simple incision without hair and proceed it between the lips with swelling on what we mentioned.
And the rule for treating swelling from above or below is to perform the work according to whatever you determine about the shape of the swelling, as it may have many variations in appearance. The surgeon devises a method using any available means.
Until it returns to its natural shape or comes close to it, and the same disease guides you on what is suitable for its treatment and tools in most cases.
Chapter Fifteen.
In connecting the eyelid to the lid edge or cornea.
This fusion may be misunderstood by many as attaching the upper lid to the white of the eye, which hinders its easy movement and impedes natural actions. It is necessary that a fold stick enter beneath the eyelid.
Lift it upwards or extend it with a hinge, then cut the attachment with a gentle clamp that doesn't have a sharp cutting edge but is slightly blunt to avoid worrying the patient as the clamp will hurt the eye if too sharp. Your cut should be like removing this attachment.
Even when the eyelid returns to its natural position and all the adhesion is healed, you can expect that after it heals completely, pour in the eye some salty water to wash it or sprinkle some camel's foot dust dissolved in water inside. Then separate the eyelid from the eye with a cotton thread.
Place over the eye a cotton ball soaked in egg white, and use the prepared camel's foot until it heals after the third day.
The sixteenth chapter.
In cutting the nail and removing its pus.
The nail can be in two forms, either it is nervous resembling a hard and thin scab, or it is not nervous, resembling a white moist dryness if it comes into contact with iron or it breaks when taken off by a hinge.
If the hinge did not stick, and both types start from the larger opening until it becomes a little by little covering the eye and preventing light and movement of the eye. The work in cutting it is that the patient places his head on your knee.
Then he opens his eyes and lifts the eyelid with your hand, then catches the nail with a very slightly bent needle and raises it up. Then he takes a thread made from horse or cow hair, or strong thread, and bends one end of the needle slightly before piercing the middle of the nail.
Then she performs it using the needle, ties the nail with the thread and raises it up. Then she cuts along the side of the nail next to the eye as if spreading it outwards with the hair, until she reaches the end of the nail, then she cuts off the rest of the nail in its root using a gentle pair of scissors or small scissors. She leaves the natural nail untouched.
So as not to expose the possibility of constant tears after cutting, the nail is extended with the needle alone or by using thread as we mentioned, then trimmed with a smooth pair of scissors whose end looks like this:.
And she protects against the scissors coming into contact with the corneal membrane causing it to tear, resulting in watering of the eye. After cutting, she puts a little powdered salt or wormwood herb in the eye and leaves it until another day, then treats her as necessary until she recovers.
If the nail is not sensitive and cannot be penetrated by a needle or a bent wire, this type of nail is often treated with medicine until it heals as described in the section. If you want to cut it, open the eye of the patient.
Take a smooth, gentle pair of scissors like this:. Gently remove the nail from above by scraping. If you see that it's breaking and tearing, scrape only with a sharp edge of your eyelid on wormwood or red wormwood or powdered salt, then pull the eye until another day.
Then, continue the operation until all is gone except if a hot tumor obstructs your view; leave it and treat the hot tumor until it heals, then resume the operation with weighing (of ingredients) until it heals, as for those prone to infection.
If it causes a terrible hurt to the eye due to being near it, suspend that nuto with a thread and cut off some of it. Do not be too intent in cutting as this may cause tearing up of tears then rinse in cold water or in water mixed with red henna or zinger until it heals.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
In cutting the varicose veins and what grows as excess flesh in the eye.
Red flesh may grow in the eyes of some people covering or getting close to, or overflowing onto the cheeks, and perhaps the eyelids turn outward resembling varicose veins.
The procedure is for the patient to lie down with his head on your pillow, then open his eyes and collect all that red flesh using tweezers matching this.
Or you might hold it with forceps or a comb. You would cut the first piece of flesh one by one, until all is cut away and be careful not to harm the eye during this process. Your cuts should either use the knife we described for cutting the hoof or a small pair of scissors. Like this as shown in this following image, when you would use the tweezers on what is about to be seen in this door.
When your cutting is complete and all varicose veins have disappeared, fill the eye with powdered salt or rinse it with red substances and other strong medicines. Then hold a piece of white cotton over the eye from outside to cool down the hot tumor.
If there is something left of the reddening, and your patient's blood has been drained out, and you fear that the hot tumor might remain, leave the eye alone and treat it with what calms down the tumor. Then proceed to work on her until she recovers. Similarly, do this process for the excess flesh that appears in the eye of this kind.
Except that you must avoid treating any weak eye through the method of imprint or display by working with iron, and do not touch anything from these operations until you see that this organ is suitable for such work.

Your work for that day should be half in the shade of the sun.
Ensure your work is precise, so that you do not cut anything other than the veins. When finished, sew up the green or red scar in the eye to eat away at whatever remains of the spouts with its sharpness. If you are unable to perform the operation completely at that moment, bandage the eye with what soothes the eye pain.
Leave him for some days until the pain subsides and the heat of the lump settles. Then resume working on this method with the same tool until this picture of pain disappears from her.

The Nineteenth Chapter.
In pushing the hair back to the nose.
Doctors call the treatment for hair, Nasour, if they treat it with fire or the hot burn medicine as previously described and it doesn't heal. If this is the case, then there's no trick other than to cut into the tumor when it matures and remove all the moisture in it or pus.
Until the bone is exposed. If the bone is exposed and you see corruption or darkness in it, remove it with this instrument depicted here:.
It is called the iron pick, made of Indian iron. Its head is shaped like a nail and it bears a delicate engraving on its surface, like that of an engraver's tool or an engraving chisel. You place it on the area of corruption in the bone and turn it between your fingers as you slightly move your hand until you know that this corruption has been removed.
You perform this action several times, then apply the medicine which is dried and tightly squeezed. If the area closes up, grows flesh there, and its healing process stops within the set period of time (presumably referring to a specific medical procedure duration), then it lasts for forty days without recurring, nor any new symptoms appearing in that area.
Know that it has healed, otherwise there's no trick other than pushing the Nasour hair back into the nasal cavity in this manner. This involves exposing the bone again either with iron or a hot medicine; if the bone is exposed, take hold of it like so:
The tip of the tool is triangular and its body conical, tapering towards the tip as you can see. Place it on the bone itself, with the part being close to your nose and slightly away from your eye. Then move your hand with the tool until the bone penetrates and reaches the sighted person.
Let him find the wind coming out if he holds his hand over his nose, then force the place with the compressed and dried medicaments as you were taught. The Thirty-first Chapter.
In extracting the teeth.
It is necessary to treat the tooth for pain by all means, refusing extraction if possible because there is no 'behind' in a tooth after extraction; it's a valuable essence. Even when extraction seems inevitable.
It is necessary if the patient decides to have their tooth extracted, that you firmly set it until the tooth stops hurting. The insufficiency of pain often deceives a patient, making them believe that the discomfort is in the correct spot. As a result, they have the afflicted area removed, but the pain persists until the diseased part is actually excised. We have witnessed this repeatedly among surgeons.

The Second and Thirty Chapters.

Chapter Thirty-One.
In braiding movable hairs with threads of silver or threads of gold.
If shown to the old hairs, they become unstable and move due to a hit or fall. The animal can't bite anything for fear of dropping it. Treatment with concentrated remedies did not help the cure.
The trick is to pull with a thread of gold or silver. Gold is better because silver corrodes and decomposes after days while gold stays the same forever, not subjecting it to that. The thread should be moderate in softness and hardness according to what can fit between the hairs.
The image of the intertwining is as follows: take the thread and insert its bend between the two correct thumbs, then weave the ends of the thread between one or more movable thumbs until the weaving reaches the correct thumb from the other side.
Then weave back to the side it started from and gently pull your hand with wisdom so that the tip does not move, and your tension is on the ends of the thread at the base of the fingers in order for them not to slip. Then cut the excess end of the thread with scissors and gather them together, tie them with a knot, and hide them between the correct finger and the movable one.
So as not to cause the tongue to swell, leave it like this tied up. If it dissolves or breaks, tighten it with another thread so you can enjoy it like this for all time. This is an image of the fingers and the method of intertwining in two correct thumbs and two movable ones as seen:
The finger might twist back one or both after falling in its place and intertwining as we described, and it remains. It is done by the craftsman who rides with a companion. They carve bone from cattle bones to make it resemble a finger and place it in the spot where the finger had been. It is tied as we said, remaining and being enjoyed like that.
Chapter 34.
In cutting the band that is placed under the tongue, it prevents speaking.
This band that is placed under the tongue may either be naturally occurring in humans, born with it, or be accidental, resulting from a healed wound.
The procedure involves opening the mouth of the patient and his head on your lap, lifting his tongue, then cutting this nervous band across until the tongue is released from holding it. If there is some hardness or complexity in it, which resulted from a healed wound, place a tool and cut it across until the band detaches and the knot dissolves.
Warn that the incision should not be too deep in the depth of the flesh, for it might cut a vessel there causing bleeding. Then wash the aftermath of the cut with rose water or vinegar and cold water, then place under the tongue a thread of cotton that is held by the slave each night.

With the edges of the skin that are under the skin from inside, until you pierce it from this side. I have gathered my skin margins and pleural margins resulting in four threads. Then, draw a double string around the needle in both sides repeatedly until the incision edges meet tightly.
Then, leaving an amount equal to the thickness of a finger, you pierce another needle and tie it with the string in the same way as the first needle. You continue this process with needles as needed until all parts of the incision are sewn up. The needles should be medium-thickness between hardness and softness.
Because the thin needles cut through flesh and cartilage very quickly, making it hard to enter the skin. Therefore, a needle should be used that is both firm and flexible in texture. It is not recommended to insert the needle too close to the edge of the skin.
So that the flesh does not cut too quickly and the wound does not open before healing, nor is it also separated by sewing so as not to prevent the wound from healing. Then trim the ends of the needles so they do not harm the patient when sleeping and provide him with gauze wicks from each side that hold the needle ends.

The Second Chapter.
In the frontal bone fracture.
The types of frontal bone fracture are numerous, with various shapes and causes. Some fractures occur due to a sword strike and may involve the entire bone up to where it ends at the sinus beneath the bone. Similarly, as it does in wood with the cutlass.
Therefore, this type of fracture is referred to as a cutlass fracture. Alternatively, the sword cuts some bone and removes only its edge without penetrating until the end of it; this type of fracture is called a blunt fracture. The injuries from these fractures can either be large or small.
The types of fracture which are brittle or compact, and whose cause is a blow with a stone or falling onto a stone or something similar, this type of fracture may either penetrate close to the membrane beneath the bone, or it may occur within the surface of the bone.
The wounds from these fractures can also be either large or small, and there is a type of fracture that is hidden within the bone in the hairline, which is a gradual expansion.
Therefore, this type of fracture is called 'hairlike' fracture. There's also a type that occurs from falling or hitting with a stone and similar objects; it penetrates into the bone surface becoming irregular in its location. It can become like brass if hit by a blow, entering part of it inside.
This is more common in wet bones like the heads of infants. All these types of fractures can have clean and unclean fragments, and we will discuss their treatment in their respective sections. We'll also identify all these types of fracture through examining them.

The arm is made up of two bones, known as the humerus and the radius. The former is smaller and lies above the thumb while the latter is larger and located beneath the smaller one at the bottom. It may be that only the major radius broke, or just the smaller radius, or both broke together.
If the smaller radius above broke, setting it is easier and noticing its correct position happens faster. If the lower radius broke, the break was bad to see and even worse if both bones broke together. And if the bone that broke was the smaller radius above.
When setting the arm, the doctor should make the process gentle and gradual so that it is corrected properly. If it's the larger radius that broke, the process should be more strenuous. If both radii are broken, then the procedure should be extremely strong.
It is necessary that the shape of the hand be placed at the elevation and extension on a pillow, with the thumb raised above all the fingers. The wrist should be lower than the rest of the fingers, and the palm should be laid flat on itself in a stable position.
Let the pillow be at his height so that the palm does not bear the burden of the wrist.
Then, the attendant of the arm extends it either from below with his hand or with a bandage and another attendant extends it from above in the same manner. Then, the doctor smoothes the bone until he can return it to the best form possible. If there are fragments in the bone fracture, they should be removed.
For each fragment, make every effort to place it back in its rightful position. If there appears a clean fragment and the skin is retracting but you don't have any intention of realigning it with force, cut into it according to the method we described before and remove it. If the fracture is accompanied by a wound, then it has been given a separate chapter.
Treatment for this begins from here; if you encounter a hot tumor in your first operation, apply an incision with the tool treated with rose oil and white beeswax. Make it medium-thick between the thickness and smoothness. Gently pull on the incision until the tumor settles.
Remove the tool and apply a pad made from dust of rhodium mixed with the whites of eggs, then lift the bones. The bone that is placed directly on the fracture should be slightly wider and stronger. Know that there will usually be seven bones in the arm.
If the fracture was within one hook or both together, then make your pulling force on the position of the fracture stronger and harder. As you pull up or down with the pull, let it lean slightly to the side as was mentioned in the first chapter.
Let the sutures that surround the fracture be wet and soft, not too hard. Use a special type of string made from goat's hair to tighten it, positioned halfway between the bone fragments as described before. Then inspect the limb and ligaments after some days.
If something needs to be fixed, such as a sore that appears in the body, it would be necessary to wash the body with warm water until the sore subsides. Let the body remain loose for one night to rest, then continue the tightening afterwards.
If the tightening has relaxed and the bone has moved or somewhat done so, fix all of that with effort, and also observe if food is being prevented from reaching the body due to excessive tightening. It would be necessary to slightly relax it and leave it for a few days until the food can reach there again, then tighten it afterwards.
If there's no reason for the illness as we mentioned, it should not heal except after twenty days or about that. Then tie the ill person to their neck and let their arm be in a moderate position, conserve their effort from chaotic movements, and have them sleep on their back.
And know that this fracture in the arm is expected to heal within thirty days or perhaps twenty-eight, and it might take as long as twenty-one days; all depends on the conditions of fluids and strength.
