Chapter Twenty-Nine.
In treating the dislocation of the elbow.
The elbow, which is often dislocated, frequently gets out of place. When it does need to be repositioned, this task is easier compared to other joints; however, when the elbow is dislocated before being returned to its proper position or while it's hot after an injury, one should hasten its return.
Repositioning the elbow involves placing the hand of the sick person on a board, stretching their arm, and having the attendant hold it. The doctor then places his hand on the joint and pushes until it returns to place, but it should be checked whether the dislocation has moved towards the palm of the hand.
The sick person should place the front of their hand on the board when stretching and retracting. If the dislocation is sticking out on the surface of the hand, they should have the bottom side of their hand on the board so that the doctor's hand can be placed right above the joint. If it returns immediately, otherwise, apply pressure with a poultice for pain relief.
Leave him alone and do not make him attempt it again, as he cannot bear it or manage its repositioning after a few days. The joint will stay out of place but does not harm the sick person unless his hand relaxes and is unable to hold anything.
Then, you will know that the nerve has been severed or there is nothing left to do about it except for tying with a sling. It may help or not at all. Once the elbow is returned into place, apply the poultice described then have them rest and keep their arm up for five days.
Then he should help and train the hand. If movement in the elbow proves difficult or if there is a piece of bone exposed, he should warm it with hot water and steam until it softens.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of breaking fingers.
The fingers may break in every direction. When one breaks towards the back or palm of the hand, extend your finger and push on it with your thumb until it returns to its original position. Then tie the tip of the finger and hang it toward the side where it broke off.
Leave it for two days, then release and stretch it until it stabilizes. If it was done at night, tie it in the same way; it will continue to improve during the day. It is exercised by movement during the day and tied at night. Do this for several days until it strengthens.
Similarly, you should do it with the hand if the finger broke towards the palm. You tie it in the direction of that side and follow your first action until it recovers. Similarly, do this for her when she breaks in other directions.
The Thirty-first Chapter.
In the treatment of breaking ribs.
If a rib or neck bone breaks, or if the complete breaking occurs, or if many ribs are removed from their places, there is no cure for it because death will hasten.
This is indicated by the urine of a sick person being discharged involuntarily, unable to hold it back. It often relaxes some of its members, either his legs or arms or both. If one rib was removed from its place, it often happens that another will be removed.
The removal of the rib to four directions will be called a galea. As for its treatment, if the galea occurred during childhood, there is no cure in it or from it completely. However, if it occurred due to falling, hitting, and similar incidents.
I have mentioned them in various forms of treatment with lengthy language that is not always beneficial. I have shortened this, providing the essential information and eliminating much of what they brought based on understanding their meaning, explaining it to them and illustrating the device differently than how they indicated and explained it.
I say that the swelling which occurs in front of the chest has no remedy and cannot be protected from it, similarly affecting both sides. Only the one occurring in the back is treated specifically as I am describing it, which involves placing the patient's face downwards.
At a level khan (a kind of stand) near a wall, spread out under it a damp mat so as not to harm his chest. Then place a standing board buried in a hole in the ground at one end of the khan towards his head and another wooden plank at the other end towards his feet on the opposite side of the khan.
And a servant holds the plank and let it not be securely fastened in the hole. And another servant holds the other plank at this manner. Then wrap it around his chest and below his elbow with a thin, smooth cloth and extend the cloth to the plank near his head and tie him there.
Then tighten another cloth above his hips and knees, and around his buttocks. Then gather all the straps together and tie them to the other plank near his feet. Afterwards, each servant tightens their plank with the strap. Do not remove the two planks from their fixed positions.
Except that they are not firmly placed as we said. The doctor puts his hands on the pin with force until it moves, or places a plank on top of it and leans against the plank with his legs until it moves. If this treatment does not work, take a plank whose length is about three arms long.
Excavate in the wall which we said should be near the elbow, where a corner of the plate enters. Then place the middle part of the plate on the crease and places his doctor's legs on the other end and pulls with great strength until it presses the carpal bone.
And return it to its place, and if you wish to make it with the rod that twists in your hand - which is to pierce the ground at the elbow's end of the mallet with two pieces of wood of one arm length, and also at his feet at the end of the mallet as well with another two pieces of wood.
And let there be a span between each piece of wood. Each piece of wood should have a hole in it for the rod to pass through. The pieces of wood are deeply anchored into the ground so tightly that they do not move, using a reed which is wound around them at the holes of the two pieces of wood.
And at its end, there is a hole that has been anchored in with a reed of one span long which is wound around it. In the other two pieces of wood, this is done similarly. Then pull the band that you tightened on the elbow's mallet near his head and the bands that are tightened on his legs near his feet.
Then he stands in front of each rod where the doctor twists his hand with the twisted stick that is wound around the rod, and the surgeon places the crease on what we have provided. This is a depiction of the mallet, the hammer, and the elbow:
And after the scab has returned and the position is leveled, it should be advisable to carry the dried bandage with the whiteness of egg whites. Then apply exertion, and place above the bandage a piece from the plate which is three fingers wide or slightly more. The length should match what fits for the crease.
On certain correct stones, then they are bound with the appropriate bandage and use gentle food as medicine until they heal. If some remnants remain in place even after healing, it is necessary to use medicines that relax and soothe, while using the board we described for a long time.
And in this case, you may use a lead plate. Sometimes there might be a remnant at the end of back surgery scars, one might think it is peeling off, but it could be excess bone that has not been removed. It should not be treated with such remedies as it might lead to death.
The thirty-first chapter.
In treating dislocated hips.
Be aware that the hip joint and the knee joint are only affected by dislocation, not by minor wear or swelling like other joints. The hip joint can be dislocated on four sides.
That is, it can dislocate towards inside and outside, as well as in front and behind. However, it more often dislocates towards inside than towards front or back. The sign of internal dislocation is that if you compare the sound leg with the diseased one, the diseased one will appear longer.
The knee is usually on the diseased side, and the healthy person cannot bend his leg at the hip joint. The position behind the hip joint is clear and distinct before the thigh bone has reached there.
Indications for dislocation to the outside are symptoms opposite these, and indications for dislocation towards front show that he spreads his leg completely until it bends without pain in the knee. If he tries to walk straight ahead, he cannot do so.
The urinary control is affected and when walking, he feels pain in his heels. A sign of someone who has undergone jaw surgery is that they cannot fully extend their knee or bend it before the bending of the curvature, and also has a shorter leg compared to the other.
The curvature is relaxed, and the thigh bone can be seen at the place of the backbone clearly. As for the types that require this surgery, if you look and find that the jaw has been worn out with its owner and he didn't try to restore it and remained in his condition, there's no cure for toothache.
It should not be subjected to surgery, and as for the one whose jaw was recently broken regardless of which type it belonged to among the four types of jaws, he should start by rotating the joint, extending it inwards and outwards, moving it right and left. It may happen.
He returned and did not need any other treatment. If he doesn't return in this way, it should be that he has two strong attendants who can extend his leg from below either with their hands or with a girth tied above the knee on his leg. Another attendant should also help him from above.
He should insert his hands under his elbows, then pull with a soft girth at the top of the thigh and hold onto one end of the girth. Another third attendant would be there, extending him either forward from the area of curvature to the front or backwards towards the back, depending on the condition.
All of them should extend him once each time so that the patient raises his body from the ground and remains suspended. This type of extension is a common feature among the four types. If the jaw returns as we have described, or otherwise, it becomes necessary for every kind of treatment specific to what I mentioned.
If the jaw is retracted inward, it should be necessary for the patient to lie on their correct side and place pillows under the hip joint between the buttock and the place below the iliac crest.
Then, the band is extended upwards from the iliac crest towards the upper body and to the side of the chest. Then another nurse takes hold with his hands and embraces the thick part of the reclinable hip while extending it as far as possible. He then returns to its place.
This type is easier than other treatment types that require this member to retract, if you are unable and refuse to proceed with this type of treatment, then it should be necessary to bind all the legs of the reclining person with a strong, soft band around the ankles and knees.
Each one of its (the reclining person's) companion is four fingers apart, and the reclinable leg is extended more than the others by two fingers. Then, the reclining person is hung on a beam in the house, which is about two arms' length from the ground.
Then, command a strong slave to embrace the hip and have another slave hold the reclining person. The slave who holds the hip is pushed with strength by the other slave, thus the joint returns quickly to its place. If retraction is inward, it follows similarly.
It should be necessary for the reclining person to lie on the stretcher as described with respect to the patient in the vessel. The band should be tightened around his reclinable leg specifically and on his chest. Then, two planks are placed, one under his feet and another at his head. A longer plank is put in the middle of the stretcher firmly attached.
If he wet bandages so as not to harm the patient, making the wood (of his legs) between his thighs in order not to be pulled down when stretching, then each slave stretches towards his side and the doctor adjusts the thigh with his hands; if it answered going back.
Otherwise, place the board and secure it as we described in the gynecological section. It should be noted that it is preferable for the patient to lie on his correct side, and if the removal is towards the front, it would be appropriate to extend the patient's leg once while lying on this exact description on the examination table.
The doctor places his right hand on the pubic area of the patient, then presses it with the other hand, and in doing so extends the pressure downwards towards the knee. If the removal is to the back, it would not be appropriate for the patient to extend downward.
He should be raised on the ground, it is preferable to place him on something solid. As well, both his legs should extend outward as described in our instructions for lying on the examination table when he is facing forward, and the bandages are tightly secured.
As we mentioned earlier, it is necessary to use the splint on the position where the joint came out. If the hip joint returns as it should, and the sign of its return will not be hidden from you, which is that both legs of the patient extend.
If you see them at the same level and the patient clenches and stretches his legs without pain, know that the limb has returned as it should. Then unite the thighs and hold the dressing, pulling tightly with a grip that doesn't allow the thigh to move in any direction.
The duration of immobilization is three or four days, then the bandage and dressing are changed. If you see them equal in size, know that the fracture has set, and allow for walking by removing the cast. If you observe any relaxation within it,
Return and re-bandage it according to your initial tightness, leaving it for three days also. Then remove it; allow walking on them for days until they strengthen sufficiently, if God wills.
The Second and Third Chapters.
In treating a dislocated knee.
The knee joint dislocates in three ways: forwards and backwards, laterally inwards and outwards, downwards towards the back. It does not dislocate in front of the patella. The sign of its dislocation is to command immobilization for walking on that leg.
If it does not stick to the thigh, know that the knee is dislocated. Force all its dislocating aspects such that the immobilization commands him to sit down with his legs extended if he can do so. Sit behind him to hold him in place and slightly back him toward the back for a little bit. Then sit yourself on his thighs.
Your back should stick to his face and place his leg between your legs. Then immobilize his knee with your hands, holding them together on his knee with the tips of your fingers. Press his side towards you with all your strength while another helper extends their leg until the knee returns to its place.
The sign of it returning is that the leg sticks to the thigh in a soft, non-resisting manner. Then compress her and stick the leg to the thigh, then tie them both with a bandage for three or four days. Then release them. It should only be used for slight walking until they strengthen sufficiently.
If returning to it as described by us proves impossible, otherwise use strong ligatures according to the description I provided for treating the hip until it returns.
The thirty-third chapter.
In the treatment of removing the heel spur.
The heel can be removed gradually or completely. Removal of the heel can either be inside or outside, and you will see that when it breaks off, the heel will protrude outwardly to the side to which it broke off.
As for the treatment of its removal, it is easier to reverse it. You should gently push with your hands and straighten it until it returns to its original position. As for treating when it breaks completely, you should have the patient sit down and be held firmly by a strong servant behind him in the middle of his back.
Then, you hold the foot with your right hand from above and with your left hand from below at the level of the ankle. Then, pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand and then with your left twice. After that, extend it with your left hand and push the foot's chest towards the leg without violence.
You perform this twice as we described. Then, in the third time, push the foot's chest towards the leg while pulling at the ankle. If it returns in one or two tries in this manner and you see that the foot is level, otherwise redo the operation on it because it will return.
If it doesn't return to you as we described and otherwise, place the patient on his back on the ground, dig deeply into the earth with a very strong stake so that it falls between his thighs. I have wrapped him tightly except for that he might not harm the patient, then fixes his knee joint.
Then another servant holds the man's hands either with his own or ties a rope around his neck. Then each servant extends his arms against his companion, with the bend of the elbow touching him so he does not sag downwards during extension, and then the doctor adjusts the jaw by his hands.
And another servant holds the correct leg downwards, then the jaw returns quickly. If the jaw has returned and you can see that it does so properly, carry the bandage and the strain, securing them tightly with straps. Place the ankle under the strap to lower it, and it would be advisable to avoid the nerve located above the heel from behind.
So that the bandage is not too tight and hurts him, leave it for two or three days. If the bandage relaxes, tighten it again then release it on the third or fourth day. The patient should refrain from walking for forty days.
If he walks before this period, it might happen that his jaw fractures and gets damaged or he won't accept the treatment afterwards. If he has a hot tumor, you should use what we described previously for calming inflammation in other parts of treatment and applying pressure until it subsides.
The thirty-fourth chapter.
In treating dislocated fingers of the hand.
It is necessary to gently and without force, adjust what has dislocated by extending the foot for a short time. This is not difficult but rather easy. If the dislocation occurred in some parts of the heel bone, it would be advisable to place the leg on a flat surface on the ground.
Or on a plank while standing as if walking, then you raise your foot onto the joint where it dislocated, and press it with your foot firmly until it returns to its place without showing any deformity in that location.
Then make a plate under his foot, so that the whole foot has two heads. Then tighten it firmly for three days. After that, let him rest and avoid walking for many days until it strengthens and he can return if God willing.
The thirty-fourth chapter.
In the types of fracture that occurs with a wound, or with a break, or both.
When something like this happens and its treatment involves embolization, it often leads to death.
Therefore, it should not be treated with embolization except by one who is cautious in his technique, long-sighted, tender and thoughtful, not careless or bold. Initially, only medications that alleviate hot tumors should be used, and patience must be exercised.
To the extent that Allah has provided safety from harm in mild disease, where a little hope for recovery appears, remove it with your power at first opportunity before the hot tumor manifests.
If the member returns as desired, use the treatment that cools hot tumors and treat the wound with suitable dry ointments. If there is a fracture involved in the fracture and it happened that there are clean fragments, remove them. And conform to what we have mentioned about simple diseases in their respective locations.
And exert yourself and purify your spirit from entering the path of deceit as you have instructed me, for this will secure your way and protect you, may God protect you.
